  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_50e3120e-a3ac-468b-865e-aeb76e55b075'

<span id="freeTextContainer10342086730437262007">Esta divertida novela relata la búsqueda de un extraterrestre que ha desaparecido, tras adoptar la apariencia de la vocalista Marta Sánchez, en la jungla urbana barcelonesa. Pero el protagonista de la narración no es Gurb, sino otro alienígena que sale en pos de él y cuyo diario constituye el esqueleto de la narración. La verdadera naturaleza del relato es de carácter satí</span>
  <span id="freeText10342086730437262007" style="display:none">Esta divertida novela relata la búsqueda de un extraterrestre que ha desaparecido, tras adoptar la apariencia de la vocalista Marta Sánchez, en la jungla urbana barcelonesa. Pero el protagonista de la narración no es Gurb, sino otro alienígena que sale en pos de él y cuyo diario constituye el esqueleto de la narración. La verdadera naturaleza del relato es de carácter satírico: Mendoza convierte esta Barcelona, a un tiempo cotidiana y absurda, en el escenario de una carnavalada que revela el verdadero rostro del hombre urbano actual.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10342086730437262007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5751798429512088246">A good, quick, light, funny, laugh-out loud read about two aliens. One, Gurb, has vanished down a back alley in Barcelona in the form of Madonna. The other, his superior, must find him. Throw in lots of satire, shape-shifting and witty observations and you have a perfect short novel.<br/><br/>Two quick things: I live in Spain but don´t trust my Spanish to read this in the original language - however, yesterday I was at a friend´s house and noticed this on the bookshelf (in castellano). Noticed that Gurb a</span>
  <span id="freeText5751798429512088246" style="display:none">A good, quick, light, funny, laugh-out loud read about two aliens. One, Gurb, has vanished down a back alley in Barcelona in the form of Madonna. The other, his superior, must find him. Throw in lots of satire, shape-shifting and witty observations and you have a perfect short novel.<br /><br />Two quick things: I live in Spain but don´t trust my Spanish to read this in the original language - however, yesterday I was at a friend´s house and noticed this on the bookshelf (in castellano). Noticed that Gurb assumes the form of Marta Sanchez, which I thought was amusing. Secondly - can anyone recommend me any more Mendoza?</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/352711-leftbanker?shelf=spanish-literature">spanish-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/352711-leftbanker?shelf=read-in-spanish">read-in-spanish</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33129389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15827145477124756594"><i>Sin Noticias de Gurb</i>* is one of those books that you could kick yourself for not thinking of the idea first—not that I could have pulled off a minor masterpiece like this but still. Written in the form of a diary of messages sent by an extraterrestrial who comes to earth, takes on human form(s), and dryly narrates what he discovers about life here on earth—or at least life in Barcelona.<br/><br/>Upon landing in Barcelona, the unnamed leader sends his underling, Gurb, out to explore the terrain. Gurb immed</span>
  <span id="freeText15827145477124756594" style="display:none"><i>Sin Noticias de Gurb</i>* is one of those books that you could kick yourself for not thinking of the idea first—not that I could have pulled off a minor masterpiece like this but still. Written in the form of a diary of messages sent by an extraterrestrial who comes to earth, takes on human form(s), and dryly narrates what he discovers about life here on earth—or at least life in Barcelona.<br /><br />Upon landing in Barcelona, the unnamed leader sends his underling, Gurb, out to explore the terrain. Gurb immediately goes AWOL and most of the book concerns the leader’s search for his partner as it takes two beings to drive their spaceship. While looking for Gurb, the leader comments on dozens and dozens of aspects of life in this bizarre corner of the world called Barcelona. <br /><br /><i>No hay en toda la Tierra gente más aficionada al trabajo que los catalanes. Si supieran hacer algo, se harían los amos del mundo.<br /><br />No one on earth enjoys work more than Catalonians. If they knew how to do something, they would rule the world.</i><br /><br />It is laugh-out-loud funny in many, many parts and even more so if you happen to be something of an outsider yourself but have been in Spain just long enough to recognize some of the more absurd aspects of modern Spanish/Catalán society. There is a little bit of Gurb in anyone who has ever lived in another country. Why hasn’t anyone thought to turn this into a movie?<br /><br />* The English title is <i>No Word from Gurb</i> which I thinks sounds funny and is a great title.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15827145477124756594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jay Green" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39595324-jay-green"><img alt="Jay Green" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524830097p2/39595324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3170456380?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2020</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3170456380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer625921692537528816">Three-and-a-half stars for an amusing little novella that plonks a couple of shape-shifting aliens down in Barcelona and constructs its plot around their separation and eventual reconciliation. A more worthwhile trope than the xenophobic aliens-are-evil-let's-kill-them-all that seems to predominate these days, this offers the chance for a gentle satire at the expense of Catalan culture. An easy read with one or two LOLs.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1727161833184293739">The second book that I've read in Spanish, this one left me feeling distinctly meh. A promising conceit - an extraterrestrial lands in Barcelona, in search of one of his crewmates and reports on the local population and customs. However, the execution, despite having the definite virtue of brevity (140 or so pages), was somewhat labored, and certainly nowhere near as amusing as the teacher who recommended the book to me seemed to find it.<br/><br/>Recommended only for those with an overwhelming interest i</span>
  <span id="freeText1727161833184293739" style="display:none">The second book that I've read in Spanish, this one left me feeling distinctly meh. A promising conceit - an extraterrestrial lands in Barcelona, in search of one of his crewmates and reports on the local population and customs. However, the execution, despite having the definite virtue of brevity (140 or so pages), was somewhat labored, and certainly nowhere near as amusing as the teacher who recommended the book to me seemed to find it.<br /><br />Recommended only for those with an overwhelming interest in Barcelona or Cataluña. Even then, you might want to go with George Orwell instead. Still, it was amusing in parts, which prevented me from giving it only a single star.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer884472816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17695839393460434104">I have mixed feelings about this one. It was quite humorous in places, but never made me laugh out loud. The diary log form was interesting, forcing a narrowed view of events; we see only as the alien sees. However, this cuts all reaction from his antics, there is no response from the locals recorded (such as when he believes losing his head numerous times in a few minutes went unnoticed and was considered normal behaviour). Amusing enough at first but increasingly it seems that no one does noti</span>
  <span id="freeText17695839393460434104" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this one. It was quite humorous in places, but never made me laugh out loud. The diary log form was interesting, forcing a narrowed view of events; we see only as the alien sees. However, this cuts all reaction from his antics, there is no response from the locals recorded (such as when he believes losing his head numerous times in a few minutes went unnoticed and was considered normal behaviour). Amusing enough at first but increasingly it seems that no one does notice. I'd rather there was more consequence in a story, or nothing he does is of any importance and reading the book becomes an exercise in waiting for the end. <br />2.5 stars; I kind of liked it</span>

<div id="review_121926876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121926876" />
    <a title="Valentin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1689063-valentin"><img alt="Valentin" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121926876?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valentin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valentin" href="/user/show/1689063-valentin">Valentin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121926876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8420315574591582851">This book is simply amazing. It's basically a diary written by an alien that comes down to Earth, Barcelona, Spain to be exact. It is a very funny book because of the way it criticizes some things that we do in society. It's also a good book to read while in Barcelona, you can connect to the places that appear in the book such as I did about a year ago. I highly recommend this book to anyone who can read Spanish or is learning Spanish in an advanced course.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40430117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40430117" />
    <a title="miaaa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/858390-miaaa"><img alt="miaaa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271144604p2/858390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40430117?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="miaaa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="miaaa" href="/user/show/858390-miaaa">miaaa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846590160" href="/book/show/1802784.No_Word_From_Gurb">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mel, Moto Moto</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to miaaa by: </span>
      Ronny
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/858390-miaaa?shelf=fictions-others">fictions-others</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40430117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12686856135911257119">'What's so funny?' A friend finally asked me since I constantly giggling and eventually burst a laugh, which I think quite loud since people in the cafe turning their heads toward our table. I need few minutes to answer it since I couldn't stop laughing. <i>'Gosh,'</i> I said, 'this Gurb's commander is knocking his female neighbour's door every five minutes asking stuff for his cooking until she gave him 2,000 pesetas and told him to go and eat in a restaurant and leave her in peace!' <br/><br/>Gurb and his comm</span>
  <span id="freeText12686856135911257119" style="display:none">'What's so funny?' A friend finally asked me since I constantly giggling and eventually burst a laugh, which I think quite loud since people in the cafe turning their heads toward our table. I need few minutes to answer it since I couldn't stop laughing. <i>'Gosh,'</i> I said, 'this Gurb's commander is knocking his female neighbour's door every five minutes asking stuff for his cooking until she gave him 2,000 pesetas and told him to go and eat in a restaurant and leave her in peace!' <br /><br />Gurb and his commander [the narrator of the story:] are shapeshifter creatures from another galaxy. Gurb took the appearance of Madonna, whilst his commander keep changing his appearances due to specific circumstances and of course after consulting the Earth catalogue. His journey to locate Gurb, who is missing, also became a learning process on Catalan exotic yet complicated lifestyle.<br /><br />However as mas Ronny said in his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40124982" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a>, for those [read: me] who have never been in Barcelona, I'm a bit lost in space. I knew nothing about the city apart of their famous and super rich football club [again soccer is not an appropiate term:] FC Barcelona. I don't think it's a coincidence I'm finishing this book whilst Barcelona is trashing Gijon at Camp Nou on Monday early morning at my local time. Despite my passion for Liverpool FC, I always wish we play as beautifully as Barcelona does first under Frank Rijkaard and now Pep Guardiola. <br /><br />Notes, find out who these characters whose appearance are copied by Gurb's commander:<br /><br />Madonna?<br />Madonna Louise Ciccone a.k.a Madonna for some people is regarded as one of the greatest pop icon, born from French-Canadian mother and Italian American father, recently divorced from one of my favourite movie director -Guy Ritchie-, and she speaks English as if she's a native Londoners. <br /><br />Gary Cooper?<br />Gary Cooper was one of American actors early in movie industrial history. To be honest I haven't watched any of his movies and even if I did, I bet I didn't know it was him. <br /><br />Cary Grant?<br />Look above. The only difference is Grant was a British-born American actor who possessed a longer list of marriages and divorces.<br /><br />Pope Pius XII?<br />Born Eugenio Maria Giuseppe Giovanni Pacelli reigned as the 260th pope, head of the Roman Catholic Church and sovereign of Vatican City, from March 2, 1939 until his death in 1958. Pius XII contributed to the rebuilding of Europe, and advocated peace and reconciliation, including lenient policies toward vanquished nations and the unification of Europe. <br /><br />Admiral Yamamoto?<br />Admiral Yamamoto was the commander-in-chief of the Combined Fleet during World War II, a graduate of the Imperial Japanese Naval Academy and a student of the U.S. Naval War College and of Harvard University. He was one of important figures in World War II history. <br /><br />Delia Smith?<br />Delia Smith is one of the majority shareholder at Norwich City F.C. She's also a UK's best-selling cookery author. No wonder Gurb's commander consults one of her recipes. <br /><br />Anyway, a friend of mine, Nicola or Niknak who is a Canaries -nickname for Norwich supporters just like her father Colin, once showed me a video when Delia cried out, well more likely screamed to the top of her lung, during the half time game against Citeh -a nickname made by some mates for Manchester City in 2005. She was probably drunk when she yelled, <i>'Message for the best football supporters in the world: we need a 12th man here. Where are you? Where are you? Let's be having you! Come on!' </i> It's more horrible when you saw it on youtube, believe me!<br /><br />Niknak hates her, well she hates everything about the board and management and the fact that they loaned their good ground talents to other clubs and have mediocre players instead. One good think Delia sacked Glenn Roeder who was responsible for all, well most, disasters occurred to Norwich City!<br /><br />***<br /><br />'Apaan sih yang segitu lucunya?' Akhirnya teman nongkrong itu bertanya padaku setelah dari tadi melihatku cekikikan hingga akhirnya tawaku pun meledak. 'Ndak, ini komandannya si Gurb mengetuk pintu apartemen tetangganya setiap lima menit minta bahan-bahan untuk masakannya. Mungkin karena kesal dan sudah larut malam, akhirnya si tetangga memberikannya uang 2.000 peseta untuk makan di restoran dan jangan mengganggunya lagi!' Jawabku setelah akhirnya bisa berhenti tertawa.<br /><br />Gurb dan komandannya, narator cerita ini, adalah dua alien dari galaksi berbeda, dan bisa berubah wujud sesuai yang mereka inginkan. Gurb menjadi Madonna, sementara komandannya selalu mengubah wujudnya sesuai mood tentunya setelah mengecek database penghuni bumi. Perjalanan sang komandan mencari Gurb yang hilang sekaligus menjadi proses pembelajaran kehidupan masyarakat Catalan yang eksotis walau rumit baginya.<br /><br />Sayangnya seperti yang disebutkan mas Ronny di <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40124982" rel="nofollow noopener">reviewnya</a> soal buku ini, aku yang belum pernah ke Barcelona merasa kebingungan akut dan terasing. Satu-satunya hal yang aku kenali dari kota ini adalah tim sepakbolanya yang kaya dan terkenal, FC Barcelona. Rasanya bukan kebetulan saat aku menyelesaikan buku ini Barcelona menghancurkan Sporting Gijon di Camp Nou. Walau aku fans berat Liverpool FC, aku selalu berharap tim kesayanganku itu bisa bermain seindah Barcelona baik ketika ditangani oleh Frank Rijkaard maupun Pep Guardiola sekarang.<br /><br />Catatan, ada baiknya mencari tahu sejumlah tokoh yang wujudnya ditiru oleh sang komandan.<br /><br />Madonna?<br />Terlahir dengan nama Madonna Louise Ciccone dari seorang ibu berdarah Perancis-Kanada dan ayah berdarah Italia-Amerika. Bagi sebagian orang dianggap ikon pop terhebat dan baru saja bercerai dari Guy Ritchie, salah satu sutradara favoritku. Logat Londoner-nya layak diganjar Oscar!<br /><br />Gary Cooper?<br />Salah satu bintang film lama Amerika. Rasanya aku belum pernah menonton film-filmnya, dan seandainya pernah aku yakin tidak mengenali kalau itu dia!<br /><br />Cary Grant?<br />Idem. Satu-satunya perbedaan adalah Grant kelahiran Inggris dan punya riwayat pernikahan dan perceraian yang lebih banyak!<br /><br />Paus Pius XII?<br />Terlahir sebagai Eugenio Maria Giuseppe Pacelli dan terpilih menjadi Paus ke 260, pemimpin Gereja Katolik Roma sejak 02 Maret 1939 hingga wafatnya di tahun 1958. Pius XII memberikan kontribusi kebangkitan kembali Eropa serta menyampaikan misi perdamaian dan rekonsiliasi [paska perang dunia:], termasuk bersikap lunak terhadap bangsa-bangsa yang menguasai dan mendorong penyatuan Eropa.<br /><br />Admiral Yamamoto?<br />Admiral Yamamoto merupakan Panglima Tertinggi Armada Gabungan Angkatan Laut Jepang saat Perang Dunia II. Lulusan Akademi Angkatan Laut Jepang, Akademi Perang Angkatan Laut Amerika serta lulusan Universitas Harvard. Salah satu tokoh penting dalam sejarah Perang Dunia II.<br /><br />Delia Smith?<br />Salah satu pemegang saham utama klub sepakbola Liga Championship Inggris, Norwich City F.C. Juga salah satu penulis buku resep terkenal di Inggris, makanya tidak heran komandan Gurb mencoba salah satu resepnya.<br /><br />Berbicara tentang Delia Smith mengingatkanku pada seorang teman dari Inggris. Nicola atau yang akrab dipanggil Niknak adalah seorang Canaries -sebutan bagi para pendukung Norwich City- sama seperti ayahnya, Colin. Pernah satu hari Niknak menunjukkan sebuah video di mana Delia Smith, di tengah jeda pertandingan antara Norwich dengan Citeh -sebutan beberapa teman bagi klub Manchester City- merebut mikrofon dan berteriak, <i>'Pesan bagi para pendukung terhebat sepakbola di dunia: kita membutuhkan orang ke-12 di sini. Di mana kalian? Di mana kalian?'</i> Diduga Delia sedang mabuk saat itu. Teriakan tersebut lebih mengerikan jika dilihat di youtube, percaya deh!<br /><br />Niknak membenci Delia, suaminya (pemegang saham mayoritas juga) dan semua orang yang duduk di manajemen klub yang meminjamkan pemain-pemain lokal mereka yang bagus ke klub lain dan memainkan pemain kelas teri. Tidak heran Norwich harus berjuang keras tidak terdegradasi ke <i>League One</i>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12686856135911257119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Elizzy B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/430209-elizzy-b"><img alt="Elizzy B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399413182p2/430209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1939758940?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizzy B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizzy B" href="/user/show/430209-elizzy-b">Elizzy B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939758940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11359615812701773287">English review below<br/><br/>Crítica en español<br/>He leído el libro por la recomendación de una buena amiga, y porque tuve la oportunidad de ver al autor este año. Es un libro muy delirante, loco, y divertido, aunque el humor, en exceso surrealista para mí, no me terminó de calar. Muy divertido repaso a la Barcelona pre-Olímpica, llena de alegría, esperanza, elementos de pueblo con sueño de metrópoli, sin el toque amargo del despetar que trajeron estas cosas en algunos...<br/>El protagonista, divertido y simple,</span>
  <span id="freeText11359615812701773287" style="display:none">English review below<br /><br />Crítica en español<br />He leído el libro por la recomendación de una buena amiga, y porque tuve la oportunidad de ver al autor este año. Es un libro muy delirante, loco, y divertido, aunque el humor, en exceso surrealista para mí, no me terminó de calar. Muy divertido repaso a la Barcelona pre-Olímpica, llena de alegría, esperanza, elementos de pueblo con sueño de metrópoli, sin el toque amargo del despetar que trajeron estas cosas en algunos...<br />El protagonista, divertido y simple, inocente, resulta un encanto delirante en el que el lector puede sentirse identificado.<br /><br />PD: si se ha vivido en Barcelona alguna vez, como me pasó a mí, es de lectura obligatoria.<br /><br />__________________________________<br /><br />English review:<br />I read the book due to the recommendation of a good friend, and because I had the opportunity to see the author this year. It is a very delirious book, crazy, and funny, although the humor, too surreal for me, unfortunately, did not really impact me. It is a very funny review to the pre-Olympic Barcelona, full of joy, hope, elements of town with dream of metropolis, without the bitter touch of the wake up that hese things brought to some people ...<br />The main character, funny and simple, innocent, is a delirious charm with who the reader can feel identified.<br /><br />PS: If you have ever lived in Barcelona, as it happened to me, it is a mandatory reading.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/890357042" />
    <a title="Michael Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6825417-michael-brown"><img alt="Michael Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326710826p2/6825417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/890357042?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Brown" href="/user/show/6825417-michael-brown">Michael Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846590160" href="/book/show/1802784.No_Word_From_Gurb">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer890357042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18113846114822787584">Does the narrator mean us? He certainly does. He's an alien searching for his pal and co-pilot Gurb, who has disappeared in Barcelona, and from that premise comes his sardonic, bewildered and occasionally scornful observations and clumsy attempts to integrate. <br/><br/>All the while I was reminded in a way of Matt Haig's fine novel <i>The Humans</i>, but Mendoza's tale is altogether more barmy and quickfire, even slapstick, especially when our narrator tries to assume human form. An early misadventure is partic</span>
  <span id="freeText18113846114822787584" style="display:none">Does the narrator mean us? He certainly does. He's an alien searching for his pal and co-pilot Gurb, who has disappeared in Barcelona, and from that premise comes his sardonic, bewildered and occasionally scornful observations and clumsy attempts to integrate. <br /><br />All the while I was reminded in a way of Matt Haig's fine novel <i>The Humans</i>, but Mendoza's tale is altogether more barmy and quickfire, even slapstick, especially when our narrator tries to assume human form. An early misadventure is particularly vivid:<br /><br /><blockquote>Enough is enough. I cannot take another step. Considerable damage to my physical state. Lost one arm, one leg and both ears. Tongue hanging out so far that after swallowing four dog turds and an unspecified number of cigarette butts have had to tie it to my belt.</blockquote><br /><br />We're with him all the way through his speedily rendered progress reports, even if he is a little wayward. Ultimately, the quest seems like a vehicle to explore the motif of the "alien out of space". In the end, he's no more absurd than anyone else trying to make it in a place that feels a million miles from home and there's even something slightly touching about how it all turns out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18113846114822787584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2774266726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774266726" />
    <a title="Sam Reaves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8537441-sam-reaves"><img alt="Sam Reaves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442459348p2/8537441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774266726?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Reaves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Reaves" href="/user/show/8537441-sam-reaves">Sam Reaves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781846590160" href="/book/show/1802784.No_Word_From_Gurb">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774266726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10328112894782832634">A curious book, published in Spain in 1990 as Sin Noticias de Gurb, social satire full of absurdist humor, sometimes very funny. Two aliens, the unnamed narrator and his companion Gurb, come to earth on an exploratory mission and land near Barcelona. They are a completely different life form but are able to assume human shape when desired. Gurb strikes out on his own and disappears; the more timid narrator sets out to find him, assuming a variety of identities which only attract attention (misce</span>
  <span id="freeText10328112894782832634" style="display:none">A curious book, published in Spain in 1990 as Sin Noticias de Gurb, social satire full of absurdist humor, sometimes very funny. Two aliens, the unnamed narrator and his companion Gurb, come to earth on an exploratory mission and land near Barcelona. They are a completely different life form but are able to assume human shape when desired. Gurb strikes out on his own and disappears; the more timid narrator sets out to find him, assuming a variety of identities which only attract attention (miscellaneous Spanish celebrities, the Pope), intermittently wreaking havoc through ignorance, inattention and miscalculation. His utterly naive observations and his wildly inappropriate attempts to imitate human behavior provide the humor. A lot of it went over my head; there are many in-jokes about Barcelona and Spanish society in the late eighties. The book is in the form of a diary, each day's entry ending with "No word from Gurb." Probably of interest mainly if you're a hard-core Barcelonaphile, or if you like off-the-wall humor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10328112894782832634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stewart" href="/user/show/447446-stewart">Stewart</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/447446-stewart?shelf=spain">spain</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48028751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8434148107083711564">If aliens were to read Eduardo Mendoza’s No Word From Gurb (1990) they may well determine that it suffers from ’structural simplicity’. While this is true, it makes it no different from most other things on Earth they are likely to discover, like family apartments and Ford Fiestas.<br/><br/>The novel, initially published in installments in the popular Spanish newspaper, El País, is told in the style of a diary and parodies the city of Barcelona in the build up to the 1992 Olympics. Each day sees a number </span>
  <span id="freeText8434148107083711564" style="display:none">If aliens were to read Eduardo Mendoza’s No Word From Gurb (1990) they may well determine that it suffers from ’structural simplicity’. While this is true, it makes it no different from most other things on Earth they are likely to discover, like family apartments and Ford Fiestas.<br /><br />The novel, initially published in installments in the popular Spanish newspaper, El País, is told in the style of a diary and parodies the city of Barcelona in the build up to the 1992 Olympics. Each day sees a number of entries, usually little more than paragraph with a time of the day attached, as one of the two aliens in the novel writes down his observations about human life while searching for his companion, the eponymous Gurb.<br /><br />Read my full review <a href="http://booklit.com/blog/2009/03/08/eduardo-mendoza-no-word-from-gurb/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

          </span>

One of the most entertaining and humurous books i have read due to that all the things the unexpirienced aliens do to try to act as normal humans meanwhile being at earth. They try to get in love without having feelings, eating in luxury restaurants when their body doesnt need any food to function, try to make friends... but what they always end up doing is embarrass themselves and being seen by other humans like crazy people. in concl</span>

They try to get in love without having feelings, eating in luxury restaurants when their body doesnt need any food to function, try to make friends... but what they always end up doing is embarrass themselves and being seen by other humans like crazy people. in conclusion, i appreciated this book a lot due to its humor and uniqueness. //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1LVpe1UPp/p5JJtZczlQrJbCjN5hC5SInRYRe8hRZCN1KTcSGMLdTLjVo2pic+LtbeHJDjV/5zC39O/MjbnClg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H4TOHvaWtzqPr5DBEtLVeFi/HBo6UjbK9K4A+pLowAW+GJB3u1vNjE5eqPIDmGc5o5xZym4mRXLeTP5N1wBmsA==')})
  }

Pero su padre quiere que vaya a la ciudad a estudiar el Bachillerato. A lo largo de la noche que precede a la partida, Daniel, insomne, con un nudo en la garganta, evocará sus correrías con sus amigos, -Roque el Moñigo y Germán el Tiñoso- a través de los campos, descubriendo el cielo y la tierra, y revivirá las andanzas de la gente sencilla de la aldea. La simpatía humana con que esa mirada infantil nos introduce en el pueblo, haciéndonos conocer toda una impresionante galería de tipos y la fuerza con que a través de rasgos frecuentemente caricaturescos se nos presentan siempre netos y vivos es uno de los grandes aciertos de esta novela. Feliz evocación de un tiempo cuyo encanto y fascinación advertimos cuando ya se nos ha escapado entre los dedos, El camino es, por su amalgama de nitidez realista, humor sutil, nostalgia contenida e Loosely based on the author’s own life, it is the story of an orphaned young woman who leaves her small town to attend university in war-ravaged Barcelona.\n\nResiding amid genteel poverty in a mysterious house on Calle de Aribau, young Andrea falls in with a wealthy band of schoolmates who provide a rich counterpoint to the squalor of her home life. As experience overtakes innocence, Andrea gradually learns the disquieting truth about the people she shares her life with: her overbearing and superstitious aunt Angustias; her nihilistic yet artistically gifted uncle Román and his violent brother Juan; and Juan’s disturbingly beautiful wife, Gloria, who secretly supports the clan with her gambling. From existential crisis to a growing maturity and resolve, Andrea’s passionate inner journey leaves her wiser, stronger, and filled with hope for the future.\n\nThe incomparable Edith Grossman’s vital new translation captures the feverish energy of Laforet’s magnificent story, showcasing its dark, powerful imagery, and its subtle humor. And Mario Vargas Llosa’s Introduction illuminates Laforet’s brilliant depiction of life during the early days of the Franco regime.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/37020.Eduardo_Mendoza">About Eduardo Mendoza</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/37020.Eduardo_Mendoza"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1249742380p3/37020.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/37020.Eduardo_Mendoza">Eduardo Mendoza
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
670
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9122837201036384029">Eduardo Mendoza studied law in the first half of the 1960s and lived in New York between 1973 and 1982, working as interpreter for the United Nations.<br/><br/>He maintained an intense relationship with novelists Juan Benet and Juan García Hortelano, poet Pere Gimferrer and writer (and neighbour) Félix de Azúa.<br/><br/>In 1975 he published his very successful first novel, <i>La verdad sobre el caso Savolta (The Truth a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9122837201036384029" style="display:none">Eduardo Mendoza studied law in the first half of the 1960s and lived in New York between 1973 and 1982, working as interpreter for the United Nations.<br /><br />He maintained an intense relationship with novelists Juan Benet and Juan García Hortelano, poet Pere Gimferrer and writer (and neighbour) Félix de Azúa.<br /><br />In 1975 he published his very successful first novel, <i>La verdad sobre el caso Savolta (The Truth about the Savolta Case)</i>, where he shows his ability to use different resources and styles. The novel is considered a precursor to the social change in the Spanish post-Franco society and the first novel of the transition to democracy. He describes the union fights from the beginning of the 20th century, showing the social, cultural and economic reality of the Barcelona at the time. A year later he was awarded the Critic Prize.<br /><br />His most acclaimed novel is probably <i>La ciudad de los prodigios (The City of Marvels</i>, 1986), about the social and urban evolution of Barcelona between the Universal Expositions of 1888 and 1929. It was adapted to the screen by Mario Camus in 1999.<br /><br />In 1996, he published his third major Barcelona novel, this time set in the 1940s, <i>Una comedia ligera (A Light Comedy)</i>.<br /><br />Also within Mendoza's work stands the saga of Ceferino, a peculiar character, a detective locked up in a mental hospital. The first of these novels, <i>El misterio de la cripta embrujada (The Mystery of the Bewitched Crypt</i>, 1979) is a parody with hilarious moments mixing detective stories with gothic narrative.<br /><br />In the second novel of the saga, <i>El laberinto de las aceitunas (The Labyrinth of the Olives</i>, 1982) he confirms his talent as parodist; the novel is one of his most successful works. The third (and last) novel of the saga, <i>La aventura del tocador de señoras (The Adventure of the Powder Room)</i> was published in 2002.<br /><br />The newspaper <i>El País</i> published two of his novels by instalments, <i>Sin noticias de Gurb ( No Word from Gurb</i>, 1990) and <i>El último trayecto de Horacio Dos (The Last Journey of Horatio Dos</i>, 2001).<br /><br />In 1990, his work in Catalan <i>Restauració</i> made its debut. He later translated it into Spanish himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9122837201036384029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3172190-sin-noticias-de-gurb">Quotes from Sin noticias de Gurb</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;No hay en todo el Universo chapuza más grande ni trasto peor hecho que el cuerpo humano. Sólo las orejas, pegadas al cráneo de cualquier modo, ya bastarían para descalificarlo. Los pies son ridículos; las tripas, asquerosas. Todas las calaveras tienen una cara de risa que no viene a cuento. De todo ello los seres humanos sólo son culpables hasta cierto punto. La verdad es que tuvieron mala suerte con la evolución.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
